        <h1 class="border-bottom-0">Pulls</h1> 
        <div class="d-none d-lg-block ml-2"> <button class="btn-link Link--secondary js-print tooltipped tooltipped-n" aria-label="Print this article"> <!-- From https://heroicons.dev/ -->

      <div id="article-contents" class="article-grid-body"> 
       <p>The Pull Request API allows you to list, view, edit, create, and even merge pull requests. Comments on pull requests can be managed via the <a href="/en/rest/reference/issues#comments">Issue Comments API</a>.</p> 
       <p>Every pull request is an issue, but not every issue is a pull request. For this reason, "shared" actions for both features, like manipulating assignees, labels and milestones, are provided within <a href="/en/rest/reference/issues">the Issues API</a>.</p> 
       <h3 id="custom-media-types-for-pull-requests"><a href="#custom-media-types-for-pull-requests">Custom media types for pull requests</a></h3> 
       <p>These are the supported media types for pull requests.</p> 
       <pre><code>application/vnd.github.VERSION.raw+json
application/vnd.github.VERSION.text+json
application/vnd.github.VERSION.html+json
application/vnd.github.VERSION.full+json
application/vnd.github.VERSION.diff
application/vnd.github.VERSION.patch
</code></pre> 
       <p>For more information, see "<a href="/en/rest/overview/media-types">Custom media types</a>."</p> <a id="diff-error"> </a>
       <p><a id="diff-error">If a diff is corrupt, contact </a><a href="https://support.github.com/contact">GitHub Support</a> or <a href="https://premium.githubsupport.com">GitHub Premium Support</a>. Include the repository name and pull request ID in your message.</p> 
       <h3 id="link-relations"><a href="#link-relations">Link Relations</a></h3> 
       <p>Pull Requests have these possible link relations:</p> 
       <table>
        <thead>
         <tr>
          <th>Name</th>
          <th>Description</th>
         </tr>
        </thead>
        <tbody>
         <tr>
          <td><code>self</code></td>
          <td>The API location of this Pull Request.</td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td><code>html</code></td>
          <td>The HTML location of this Pull Request.</td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td><code>issue</code></td>
          <td>The API location of this Pull Request's <a href="/en/rest/reference/issues">Issue</a>.</td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td><code>comments</code></td>
          <td>The API location of this Pull Request's <a href="/en/rest/reference/issues#comments">Issue comments</a>.</td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td><code>review_comments</code></td>
          <td>The API location of this Pull Request's <a href="/en/rest/reference/pulls#comments">Review comments</a>.</td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td><code>review_comment</code></td>
          <td>The <a href="/en/rest#hypermedia">URL template</a> to construct the API location for a <a href="/en/rest/reference/pulls#comments">Review comment</a> in this Pull Request's repository.</td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td><code>commits</code></td>
          <td>The API location of this Pull Request's <a href="#list-commits-on-a-pull-request">commits</a>.</td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td><code>statuses</code></td>
          <td>The API location of this Pull Request's <a href="/en/rest/reference/repos#statuses">commit statuses</a>, which are the statuses of its <code>head</code> branch.</td>
         </tr>
        </tbody>
       </table> 
       <div> 
        <div> 
         <h3 id="list-pull-requests" class="pt-3"> <a href="#list-pull-requests">List pull requests</a> </h3> 
         <p>Draft pull requests are available in public repositories with GitHub Free and GitHub Free for organizations, GitHub Pro, and legacy per-repository billing plans, and in public and private repositories with GitHub Team and GitHub Enterprise Cloud. For more information, see <a href="https://help.github.com/github/getting-started-with-github/githubs-products">GitHub's products</a> in the GitHub Help documentation.</p> 
        </div> 
        <pre><code><span class="color-bg-info-inverse color-text-inverse rounded-1 px-2 py-1" style="text-transform: uppercase">get</span> /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls</code></pre> 
        <div> 
         <h4 id="list-pull-requests--parameters"> <a href="#list-pull-requests--parameters">Parameters</a> </h4> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Name</th> 
            <th>Type</th> 
            <th>In</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> <!--
            Previews require an `accept` header. These used to be documented
            as `operation.parameters` but have moved to `operation.x-github.previews`
          --> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>accept</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">header</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p> Setting to <code>application/vnd.github.v3+json</code> is recommended. </p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>owner</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>repo</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>state</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">query</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>Either <code>open</code>, <code>closed</code>, or <code>all</code> to filter by state.</p> Default: <code>open</code> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>head</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">query</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>Filter pulls by head user or head organization and branch name in the format of <code>user:ref-name</code> or <code>organization:ref-name</code>. For example: <code>github:new-script-format</code> or <code>octocat:test-branch</code>.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>base</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">query</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>Filter pulls by base branch name. Example: <code>gh-pages</code>.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>sort</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">query</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>What to sort results by. Can be either <code>created</code>, <code>updated</code>, <code>popularity</code> (comment count) or <code>long-running</code> (age, filtering by pulls updated in the last month).</p> Default: <code>created</code> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>direction</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">query</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>The direction of the sort. Can be either <code>asc</code> or <code>desc</code>. Default: <code>desc</code> when sort is <code>created</code> or sort is not specified, otherwise <code>asc</code>.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>per_page</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">query</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>Results per page (max 100).</p> Default: <code>30</code> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>page</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">query</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>Page number of the results to fetch.</p> Default: <code>1</code> </td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
         <h4 id="list-pull-requests--code-samples"> <a href="#list-pull-requests--code-samples">Code samples</a> </h4> 
         <h5> Shell </h5> 
         <pre><code class="hljs language-shell">curl \
  -H "Accept: application/vnd.github.v3+json" \
  https://api.github.com/repos/octocat/hello-world/pulls</code></pre> 
         <h5> JavaScript (<a href="https://github.com/octokit/core.js#readme">@octokit/core.js</a>) </h5> 
         <pre><code class="hljs language-javascript"><span class="hljs-keyword">await</span> octokit.request(<span class="hljs-string">'GET /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls'</span>, {
  <span class="hljs-attr">owner</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'octocat'</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">repo</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'hello-world'</span>
})
</code></pre>

         <pre><code>Status: 200 OK</code></pre>

       <div> 
        <div> 
         <h3 id="create-a-pull-request" class="pt-3"> <a href="#create-a-pull-request">Create a pull request</a> </h3> 
         <p>Draft pull requests are available in public repositories with GitHub Free and GitHub Free for organizations, GitHub Pro, and legacy per-repository billing plans, and in public and private repositories with GitHub Team and GitHub Enterprise Cloud. For more information, see <a href="https://help.github.com/github/getting-started-with-github/githubs-products">GitHub's products</a> in the GitHub Help documentation.</p> 
         <p>To open or update a pull request in a public repository, you must have write access to the head or the source branch. For organization-owned repositories, you must be a member of the organization that owns the repository to open or update a pull request.</p> 
         <p>You can create a new pull request.</p> 
         <p>This endpoint triggers <a href="https://docs.github.com/en/github/managing-subscriptions-and-notifications-on-github/about-notifications">notifications</a>. Creating content too quickly using this endpoint may result in abuse rate limiting. See "<a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/overview/resources-in-the-rest-api#abuse-rate-limits">Abuse rate limits</a>" and "<a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/guides/best-practices-for-integrators#dealing-with-rate-limits">Dealing with abuse rate limits</a>" for details.</p> 
        </div> 
        <pre><code><span class="color-bg-info-inverse color-text-inverse rounded-1 px-2 py-1" style="text-transform: uppercase">post</span> /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls</code></pre> 
        <div> 
         <h4 id="create-a-pull-request--parameters"> <a href="#create-a-pull-request--parameters">Parameters</a> </h4> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Name</th> 
            <th>Type</th> 
            <th>In</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> <!--
            Previews require an `accept` header. These used to be documented
            as `operation.parameters` but have moved to `operation.x-github.previews`
          --> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>accept</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">header</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p> Setting to <code>application/vnd.github.v3+json</code> is recommended. </p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>owner</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>repo</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>title</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>The title of the new pull request.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>head</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p><strong>Required</strong>. The name of the branch where your changes are implemented. For cross-repository pull requests in the same network, namespace <code>head</code> with a user like this: <code>username:branch</code>.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>base</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p><strong>Required</strong>. The name of the branch you want the changes pulled into. This should be an existing branch on the current repository. You cannot submit a pull request to one repository that requests a merge to a base of another repository.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>body</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>The contents of the pull request.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>maintainer_can_modify</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">boolean</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>Indicates whether <a href="https://help.github.com/articles/allowing-changes-to-a-pull-request-branch-created-from-a-fork/">maintainers can modify</a> the pull request.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>draft</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">boolean</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>Indicates whether the pull request is a draft. See "<a href="https://help.github.com/en/articles/about-pull-requests#draft-pull-requests">Draft Pull Requests</a>" in the GitHub Help documentation to learn more.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>issue</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
         <h4 id="create-a-pull-request--code-samples"> <a href="#create-a-pull-request--code-samples">Code samples</a> </h4> 
         <h5> Shell </h5> 
         <pre><code class="hljs language-shell">curl \
  -X POST \
  -H "Accept: application/vnd.github.v3+json" \
  https://api.github.com/repos/octocat/hello-world/pulls \
  -d '{"head":"head","base":"base"}'</code></pre> 
         <h5> JavaScript (<a href="https://github.com/octokit/core.js#readme">@octokit/core.js</a>) </h5> 
         <pre><code class="hljs language-javascript"><span class="hljs-keyword">await</span> octokit.request(<span class="hljs-string">'POST /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls'</span>, {
  <span class="hljs-attr">owner</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'octocat'</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">repo</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'hello-world'</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">head</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'head'</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">base</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'base'</span>
})
</code></pre>

        <div> 
         <h3 id="get-a-pull-request" class="pt-3"> <a href="#get-a-pull-request">Get a pull request</a> </h3> 
         <p>Draft pull requests are available in public repositories with GitHub Free and GitHub Free for organizations, GitHub Pro, and legacy per-repository billing plans, and in public and private repositories with GitHub Team and GitHub Enterprise Cloud. For more information, see <a href="https://help.github.com/github/getting-started-with-github/githubs-products">GitHub's products</a> in the GitHub Help documentation.</p> 
         <p>Lists details of a pull request by providing its number.</p> 
         <p>When you get, <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/reference/pulls/#create-a-pull-request">create</a>, or <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/reference/pulls#update-a-pull-request">edit</a> a pull request, GitHub creates a merge commit to test whether the pull request can be automatically merged into the base branch. This test commit is not added to the base branch or the head branch. You can review the status of the test commit using the <code>mergeable</code> key. For more information, see "<a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/guides/getting-started-with-the-git-database-api#checking-mergeability-of-pull-requests">Checking mergeability of pull requests</a>".</p> 
         <p>The value of the <code>mergeable</code> attribute can be <code>true</code>, <code>false</code>, or <code>null</code>. If the value is <code>null</code>, then GitHub has started a background job to compute the mergeability. After giving the job time to complete, resubmit the request. When the job finishes, you will see a non-<code>null</code> value for the <code>mergeable</code> attribute in the response. If <code>mergeable</code> is <code>true</code>, then <code>merge_commit_sha</code> will be the SHA of the <em>test</em> merge commit.</p> 
         <p>The value of the <code>merge_commit_sha</code> attribute changes depending on the state of the pull request. Before merging a pull request, the <code>merge_commit_sha</code> attribute holds the SHA of the <em>test</em> merge commit. After merging a pull request, the <code>merge_commit_sha</code> attribute changes depending on how you merged the pull request:</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li>If merged as a <a href="https://help.github.com/articles/about-merge-methods-on-github/">merge commit</a>, <code>merge_commit_sha</code> represents the SHA of the merge commit.</li> 
          <li>If merged via a <a href="https://help.github.com/articles/about-merge-methods-on-github/#squashing-your-merge-commits">squash</a>, <code>merge_commit_sha</code> represents the SHA of the squashed commit on the base branch.</li> 
          <li>If <a href="https://help.github.com/articles/about-merge-methods-on-github/#rebasing-and-merging-your-commits">rebased</a>, <code>merge_commit_sha</code> represents the commit that the base branch was updated to.</li> 
         </ul> 
         <p>Pass the appropriate <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/overview/media-types/#commits-commit-comparison-and-pull-requests">media type</a> to fetch diff and patch formats.</p> 
        </div> 
        <pre><code><span class="color-bg-info-inverse color-text-inverse rounded-1 px-2 py-1" style="text-transform: uppercase">get</span> /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/{pull_number}</code></pre> 
        <div> 
         <h4 id="get-a-pull-request--parameters"> <a href="#get-a-pull-request--parameters">Parameters</a> </h4> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Name</th> 
            <th>Type</th> 
            <th>In</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> <!--
            Previews require an `accept` header. These used to be documented
            as `operation.parameters` but have moved to `operation.x-github.previews`
          --> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>accept</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">header</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p> Setting to <code>application/vnd.github.v3+json</code> is recommended. </p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>owner</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>repo</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>pull_number</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
         <h4 id="get-a-pull-request--code-samples"> <a href="#get-a-pull-request--code-samples">Code samples</a> </h4> 
         <h5> Shell </h5> 
         <pre><code class="hljs language-shell">curl \
  -H "Accept: application/vnd.github.v3+json" \
  https://api.github.com/repos/octocat/hello-world/pulls/42</code></pre> 
         <h5> JavaScript (<a href="https://github.com/octokit/core.js#readme">@octokit/core.js</a>) </h5> 
         <pre><code class="hljs language-javascript"><span class="hljs-keyword">await</span> octokit.request(<span class="hljs-string">'GET /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/{pull_number}'</span>, {
  <span class="hljs-attr">owner</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'octocat'</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">repo</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'hello-world'</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">pull_number</span>: <span class="hljs-number">42</span>
})
</code></pre> 
         <h4>Pass the appropriate [media type](https://docs.github.com/rest/overview/media-types/#commits-commit-comparison-and-pull-requests) to fetch diff and patch formats.</h4> 
         <pre><code>Status: 200 OK</code></pre> 
         <div class="height-constrained-code-block">
          <pre><code class="hljs language-json">{
  <span class="hljs-attr">"url"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"https://api.github.com/repos/octocat/Hello-World/pulls/1347"</span>,

        <div> 
         <h3 id="update-a-pull-request" class="pt-3"> <a href="#update-a-pull-request">Update a pull request</a> </h3> 
         <p>Draft pull requests are available in public repositories with GitHub Free and GitHub Free for organizations, GitHub Pro, and legacy per-repository billing plans, and in public and private repositories with GitHub Team and GitHub Enterprise Cloud. For more information, see <a href="https://help.github.com/github/getting-started-with-github/githubs-products">GitHub's products</a> in the GitHub Help documentation.</p> 
         <p>To open or update a pull request in a public repository, you must have write access to the head or the source branch. For organization-owned repositories, you must be a member of the organization that owns the repository to open or update a pull request.</p> 
        </div> 
        <pre><code><span class="color-bg-info-inverse color-text-inverse rounded-1 px-2 py-1" style="text-transform: uppercase">patch</span> /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/{pull_number}</code></pre> 
        <div> 
         <h4 id="update-a-pull-request--parameters"> <a href="#update-a-pull-request--parameters">Parameters</a> </h4> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Name</th> 
            <th>Type</th> 
            <th>In</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> <!--
            Previews require an `accept` header. These used to be documented
            as `operation.parameters` but have moved to `operation.x-github.previews`
          --> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>accept</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">header</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p> Setting to <code>application/vnd.github.v3+json</code> is recommended. </p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>owner</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>repo</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>pull_number</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>title</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>The title of the pull request.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>body</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>The contents of the pull request.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>state</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>State of this Pull Request. Either <code>open</code> or <code>closed</code>.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>base</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>The name of the branch you want your changes pulled into. This should be an existing branch on the current repository. You cannot update the base branch on a pull request to point to another repository.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>maintainer_can_modify</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">boolean</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>Indicates whether <a href="https://help.github.com/articles/allowing-changes-to-a-pull-request-branch-created-from-a-fork/">maintainers can modify</a> the pull request.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
         <h4 id="update-a-pull-request--code-samples"> <a href="#update-a-pull-request--code-samples">Code samples</a> </h4> 
         <h5> Shell </h5> 
         <pre><code class="hljs language-shell">curl \
  -X PATCH \
  -H "Accept: application/vnd.github.v3+json" \
  https://api.github.com/repos/octocat/hello-world/pulls/42 \
  -d '{"title":"title"}'</code></pre> 
         <h5> JavaScript (<a href="https://github.com/octokit/core.js#readme">@octokit/core.js</a>) </h5> 
         <pre><code class="hljs language-javascript"><span class="hljs-keyword">await</span> octokit.request(<span class="hljs-string">'PATCH /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/{pull_number}'</span>, {
  <span class="hljs-attr">owner</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'octocat'</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">repo</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'hello-world'</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">pull_number</span>: <span class="hljs-number">42</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">title</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'title'</span>
})
</code></pre>

       <div> 
        <div> 
         <h3 id="list-commits-on-a-pull-request" class="pt-3"> <a href="#list-commits-on-a-pull-request">List commits on a pull request</a> </h3> 
         <p>Lists a maximum of 250 commits for a pull request. To receive a complete commit list for pull requests with more than 250 commits, use the <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/reference/repos#list-commits">List commits</a> endpoint.</p> 
        </div> 
        <pre><code><span class="color-bg-info-inverse color-text-inverse rounded-1 px-2 py-1" style="text-transform: uppercase">get</span> /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/{pull_number}/commits</code></pre> 
        <div> 
         <h4 id="list-commits-on-a-pull-request--parameters"> <a href="#list-commits-on-a-pull-request--parameters">Parameters</a> </h4> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Name</th> 
            <th>Type</th> 
            <th>In</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> <!--
            Previews require an `accept` header. These used to be documented
            as `operation.parameters` but have moved to `operation.x-github.previews`
          --> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>accept</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">header</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p> Setting to <code>application/vnd.github.v3+json</code> is recommended. </p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>owner</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>repo</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>pull_number</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>per_page</code></td>

           </tr>

        <div> 
         <h3 id="merge-a-pull-request" class="pt-3"> <a href="#merge-a-pull-request">Merge a pull request</a> </h3> 
         <p>This endpoint triggers <a href="https://docs.github.com/github/managing-subscriptions-and-notifications-on-github/about-notifications">notifications</a>. Creating content too quickly using this endpoint may result in abuse rate limiting. See "<a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/overview/resources-in-the-rest-api#abuse-rate-limits">Abuse rate limits</a>" and "<a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/guides/best-practices-for-integrators#dealing-with-abuse-rate-limits">Dealing with abuse rate limits</a>" for details.</p> 
        </div> 
        <pre><code><span class="color-bg-info-inverse color-text-inverse rounded-1 px-2 py-1" style="text-transform: uppercase">put</span> /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/{pull_number}/merge</code></pre> 
        <div> 
         <h4 id="merge-a-pull-request--parameters"> <a href="#merge-a-pull-request--parameters">Parameters</a> </h4> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Name</th> 
            <th>Type</th> 
            <th>In</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> <!--
            Previews require an `accept` header. These used to be documented
            as `operation.parameters` but have moved to `operation.x-github.previews`
          --> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>accept</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">header</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p> Setting to <code>application/vnd.github.v3+json</code> is recommended. </p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>owner</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>repo</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>pull_number</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>commit_title</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>Title for the automatic commit message.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>commit_message</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>Extra detail to append to automatic commit message.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>sha</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>SHA that pull request head must match to allow merge.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>merge_method</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>Merge method to use. Possible values are <code>merge</code>, <code>squash</code> or <code>rebase</code>. Default is <code>merge</code>.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
         <h4 id="merge-a-pull-request--code-samples"> <a href="#merge-a-pull-request--code-samples">Code samples</a> </h4> 
         <h5> Shell </h5> 
         <pre><code class="hljs language-shell">curl \
  -X PUT \
  -H "Accept: application/vnd.github.v3+json" \
  https://api.github.com/repos/octocat/hello-world/pulls/42/merge \
  -d '{"commit_title":"commit_title"}'</code></pre> 
         <h5> JavaScript (<a href="https://github.com/octokit/core.js#readme">@octokit/core.js</a>) </h5> 
         <pre><code class="hljs language-javascript"><span class="hljs-keyword">await</span> octokit.request(<span class="hljs-string">'PUT /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/{pull_number}/merge'</span>, {
  <span class="hljs-attr">owner</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'octocat'</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">repo</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'hello-world'</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">pull_number</span>: <span class="hljs-number">42</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">commit_title</span>: <span class="hljs-string">'commit_title'</span>
})
</code></pre> 
         <h4>if merge was successful</h4> 
         <pre><code>Status: 200 OK</code></pre> 
         <div class="height-constrained-code-block">
          <pre><code class="hljs language-json">{
  <span class="hljs-attr">"sha"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"6dcb09b5b57875f334f61aebed695e2e4193db5e"</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">"merged"</span>: <span class="hljs-literal">true</span>,
  <span class="hljs-attr">"message"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"Pull Request successfully merged"</span>
}
</code></pre>
         </div> 
         <h4>Forbidden</h4> 
         <pre><code>Status: 403 Forbidden</code></pre> 
         <div class="height-constrained-code-block"></div> 
         <h4>Resource not found</h4> 
         <pre><code>Status: 404 Not Found</code></pre> 
         <div class="height-constrained-code-block"></div> 
         <h4>Method Not Allowed if merge cannot be performed</h4> 
         <pre><code>Status: 405 Method Not Allowed</code></pre> 
         <div class="height-constrained-code-block">
          <pre><code class="hljs language-json">{
  <span class="hljs-attr">"message"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"Pull Request is not mergeable"</span>
}
</code></pre>
         </div> 
         <h4>Conflict if sha was provided and pull request head did not match</h4> 
         <pre><code>Status: 409 Conflict</code></pre> 
         <div class="height-constrained-code-block">
          <pre><code class="hljs language-json">{
  <span class="hljs-attr">"message"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"Head branch was modified. Review and try the merge again."</span>
}
</code></pre>
         </div> 
         <h4>Validation failed</h4> 
         <pre><code>Status: 422 Unprocessable Entity</code></pre> 
         <div class="height-constrained-code-block"></div> 
         <h4>Notes</h4> 
         <ul class="mt-2"> 
          <li><a href="/en/developers/apps">Works with GitHub Apps</a></li> 
         </ul> 
        </div> 
        <hr> 
       </div> 
       <div> 
        <div> 
         <h3 id="update-a-pull-request-branch" class="pt-3"> <a href="#update-a-pull-request-branch">Update a pull request branch</a> </h3> 
         <p>Updates the pull request branch with the latest upstream changes by merging HEAD from the base branch into the pull request branch.</p> 
        </div> 
        <pre><code><span class="color-bg-info-inverse color-text-inverse rounded-1 px-2 py-1" style="text-transform: uppercase">put</span> /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/{pull_number}/update-branch</code></pre> 
        <div> 
         <h4 id="update-a-pull-request-branch--parameters"> <a href="#update-a-pull-request-branch--parameters">Parameters</a> </h4> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Name</th> 
            <th>Type</th> 
            <th>In</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> <!--
            Previews require an `accept` header. These used to be documented
            as `operation.parameters` but have moved to `operation.x-github.previews`
          --> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>accept</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">header</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p> This API is under preview and subject to change. <a href="#update-a-pull-request-branch-preview-notices"> See preview notice </a> </p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>owner</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>repo</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>pull_number</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>expected_head_sha</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>The expected SHA of the pull request's HEAD ref. This is the most recent commit on the pull request's branch. If the expected SHA does not match the pull request's HEAD, you will receive a <code>422 Unprocessable Entity</code> status. You can use the "<a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/reference/repos#list-commits">List commits</a>" endpoint to find the most recent commit SHA. Default: SHA of the pull request's current HEAD ref.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
         <h4 id="update-a-pull-request-branch--code-samples"> <a href="#update-a-pull-request-branch--code-samples">Code samples</a> </h4>

         <h4 id="update-a-pull-request-branch-preview-notices"> Preview notice </h4> 
         <div class="extended-markdown note border rounded-1 mb-4 p-3 color-border-info color-bg-info f5"> 
          <p>Updating the pull request branch with latest upstream changes is currently available for developers to preview. To access this new endpoint during the preview period, you must provide a custom <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/overview/media-types">media type</a> in the <code>Accept</code> header:</p> 
          <pre><code class="hljs language-shell">application/vnd.github.lydian-preview+json</code></pre> ?? This header is <strong>required</strong>.

       <h2 id="reviews"><a href="#reviews">Reviews</a></h2> 
       <p>Pull Request Reviews are groups of Pull Request Review Comments on the Pull Request, grouped together with a state and optional body comment.</p> 
       <div> 
        <div>

       <div> 
        <div> 
         <h3 id="create-a-review-for-a-pull-request" class="pt-3"> <a href="#create-a-review-for-a-pull-request">Create a review for a pull request</a> </h3> 
         <p>This endpoint triggers <a href="https://docs.github.com/en/github/managing-subscriptions-and-notifications-on-github/about-notifications">notifications</a>. Creating content too quickly using this endpoint may result in abuse rate limiting. See "<a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/overview/resources-in-the-rest-api#abuse-rate-limits">Abuse rate limits</a>" and "<a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/guides/best-practices-for-integrators#dealing-with-rate-limits">Dealing with abuse rate limits</a>" for details.</p> 
         <p>Pull request reviews created in the <code>PENDING</code> state do not include the <code>submitted_at</code> property in the response.</p> 
         <p><strong>Note:</strong> To comment on a specific line in a file, you need to first determine the <em>position</em> of that line in the diff. The GitHub REST API v3 offers the <code>application/vnd.github.v3.diff</code> <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/overview/media-types#commits-commit-comparison-and-pull-requests">media type</a>. To see a pull request diff, add this media type to the <code>Accept</code> header of a call to the <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/reference/pulls#get-a-pull-request">single pull request</a> endpoint.</p> 
         <p>The <code>position</code> value equals the number of lines down from the first "@@" hunk header in the file you want to add a comment. The line just below the "@@" line is position 1, the next line is position 2, and so on. The position in the diff continues to increase through lines of whitespace and additional hunks until the beginning of a new file.</p> 
        </div> 
        <pre><code><span class="color-bg-info-inverse color-text-inverse rounded-1 px-2 py-1" style="text-transform: uppercase">post</span> /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/{pull_number}/reviews</code></pre> 
        <div> 
         <h4 id="create-a-review-for-a-pull-request--parameters"> <a href="#create-a-review-for-a-pull-request--parameters">Parameters</a> </h4> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Name</th> 
            <th>Type</th> 
            <th>In</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> <!--
            Previews require an `accept` header. These used to be documented
            as `operation.parameters` but have moved to `operation.x-github.previews`
          --> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>accept</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">header</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p> Setting to <code>application/vnd.github.v3+json</code> is recommended. </p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>owner</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>repo</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>pull_number</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>commit_id</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>The SHA of the commit that needs a review. Not using the latest commit SHA may render your review comment outdated if a subsequent commit modifies the line you specify as the <code>position</code>. Defaults to the most recent commit in the pull request when you do not specify a value.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>body</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p><strong>Required</strong> when using <code>REQUEST_CHANGES</code> or <code>COMMENT</code> for the <code>event</code> parameter. The body text of the pull request review.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>event</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>The review action you want to perform. The review actions include: <code>APPROVE</code>, <code>REQUEST_CHANGES</code>, or <code>COMMENT</code>. By leaving this blank, you set the review action state to <code>PENDING</code>, which means you will need to <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/reference/pulls#submit-a-review-for-a-pull-request">submit the pull request review</a> when you are ready.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>comments</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">array of objects</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>Use the following table to specify the location, destination, and contents of the draft review comment.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr style="border: none;"> 
            <td colspan="4" class="has-nested-table"> 
             <details> <summary class="color-text-secondary"><h4 id="comments-items">Properties of the <code>comments</code> items</h4></summary> 
              <table> 
               <tbody> 
                <tr> 
                 <td class="opacity-60"><code>path</code> (string)</td> 
                 <td class="opacity-60"><p><strong>Required</strong>. The relative path to the file that necessitates a review comment.</p></td> 
                </tr> 
                <tr> 
                 <td class="opacity-60"><code>position</code> (integer)</td> 
                 <td class="opacity-60"><p>The position in the diff where you want to add a review comment. Note this value is not the same as the line number in the file. For help finding the position value, read the note below.</p></td> 
                </tr> 
                <tr> 
                 <td class="opacity-60"><code>body</code> (string)</td> 
                 <td class="opacity-60"><p><strong>Required</strong>. Text of the review comment.</p></td> 
                </tr> 
                <tr> 
                 <td class="opacity-60"><code>line</code> (integer)</td> 
                 <td class="opacity-60"></td> 
                </tr> 
                <tr> 
                 <td class="opacity-60"><code>side</code> (string)</td> 
                 <td class="opacity-60"></td> 
                </tr> 
                <tr> 
                 <td class="opacity-60"><code>start_line</code> (integer)</td> 
                 <td class="opacity-60"></td> 
                </tr> 
                <tr> 
                 <td class="opacity-60"><code>start_side</code> (string)</td> 
                 <td class="opacity-60"></td> 
                </tr> 
               </tbody> 
              </table> 
             </details> </td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table>

         <h3 id="dismiss-a-review-for-a-pull-request" class="pt-3"> <a href="#dismiss-a-review-for-a-pull-request">Dismiss a review for a pull request</a> </h3> 
         <p><strong>Note:</strong> To dismiss a pull request review on a <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/reference/repos#branches">protected branch</a>, you must be a repository administrator or be included in the list of people or teams who can dismiss pull request reviews.</p> 
        </div> 
        <pre><code><span class="color-bg-info-inverse color-text-inverse rounded-1 px-2 py-1" style="text-transform: uppercase">put</span> /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/{pull_number}/reviews/{review_id}/dismissals</code></pre> 
        <div>

         <h3 id="submit-a-review-for-a-pull-request" class="pt-3"> <a href="#submit-a-review-for-a-pull-request">Submit a review for a pull request</a> </h3> 
        </div> 
        <pre><code><span class="color-bg-info-inverse color-text-inverse rounded-1 px-2 py-1" style="text-transform: uppercase">post</span> /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/{pull_number}/reviews/{review_id}/events</code></pre> 
        <div> 
         <h4 id="submit-a-review-for-a-pull-request--parameters"> <a href="#submit-a-review-for-a-pull-request--parameters">Parameters</a> </h4> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Name</th> 
            <th>Type</th> 
            <th>In</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> <!--
            Previews require an `accept` header. These used to be documented
            as `operation.parameters` but have moved to `operation.x-github.previews`
          --> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>accept</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">header</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p> Setting to <code>application/vnd.github.v3+json</code> is recommended. </p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>owner</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>repo</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>pull_number</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>review_id</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>review_id parameter</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>body</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>The body text of the pull request review</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>event</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p><strong>Required</strong>. The review action you want to perform. The review actions include: <code>APPROVE</code>, <code>REQUEST_CHANGES</code>, or <code>COMMENT</code>. When you leave this blank, the API returns <em>HTTP 422 (Unrecognizable entity)</em> and sets the review action state to <code>PENDING</code>, which means you will need to re-submit the pull request review using a review action.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table>

       <h2 id="review-comments"><a href="#review-comments">Review comments</a></h2> 
       <p>Pull request review comments are comments on a portion of the unified diff made during a pull request review. Commit comments and issue comments are different from pull request review comments. You apply commit comments directly to a commit and you apply issue comments without referencing a portion of the unified diff. For more information, see "<a href="/en/rest/reference/git#create-a-commit">Create a commit comment</a>" and "<a href="/en/rest/reference/issues#create-an-issue-comment">Create an issue comment</a>."</p> 
       <h3 id="custom-media-types-for-pull-request-review-comments"><a href="#custom-media-types-for-pull-request-review-comments">Custom media types for pull request review comments</a></h3> 
       <p>These are the supported media types for pull request review comments.</p> 
       <pre><code>application/vnd.github.VERSION.raw+json
application/vnd.github.VERSION.text+json
application/vnd.github.VERSION.html+json
application/vnd.github.VERSION.full+json
</code></pre> 
       <p>For more information, see "<a href="/en/rest/overview/media-types">Custom media types</a>."</p> 
       <div> 
        <div> 
         <h3 id="list-review-comments-in-a-repository" class="pt-3"> <a href="#list-review-comments-in-a-repository">List review comments in a repository</a> </h3> 
         <p>Lists review comments for all pull requests in a repository. By default, review comments are in ascending order by ID.</p> 
        </div> 
        <pre><code><span class="color-bg-info-inverse color-text-inverse rounded-1 px-2 py-1" style="text-transform: uppercase">get</span> /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/comments</code></pre>

           </tr>

         <h4 id="list-review-comments-in-a-repository-preview-notices"> Preview notices </h4> 
         <div class="extended-markdown note border rounded-1 mb-4 p-3 color-border-info color-bg-info f5"> 
          <p>Multi-line comments in a pull request diff is currently available for developers to preview. During the preview period, these response fields may change without advance notice. See the <a href="https://developer.github.com/changes/2019-10-03-multi-line-comments">blog post</a> for more information.</p> 
          <p>To create multi-line comments or see multi-line comments with the new supported fields during the preview period, you must provide a custom <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/overview/media-types">media type</a> in the <code>Accept</code> header:</p> 
          <pre><code class="hljs language-shell">application/vnd.github.comfort-fade-preview+json</code></pre> 
          <p>To show multi-line comment-supported fields in the response, use the <code>comfort-fade</code> preview header and the <code>line</code> parameter.</p> 
          <p>If you use the <code>comfort-fade</code> preview header, your response will show:</p> 
          <ul> 
           <li>For multi-line comments, values for <code>start_line</code>, <code>original_start_line</code>, <code>start_side</code>, <code>line</code>, <code>original_line</code>, and <code>side</code>.</li> 
           <li>For single-line comments, values for <code>line</code>, <code>original_line</code>, and <code>side</code> and a <code>null</code> value for <code>start_line</code>, <code>original_start_line</code>, and <code>start_side</code>.</li> 
          </ul> 
          <p>If you don't use the <code>comfort-fade</code> preview header, multi-line and single-line comments will appear the same way in the response with a single <code>position</code> attribute. Your response will show:</p> 
          <ul> 
           <li>For multi-line comments, the last line of the comment range for the <code>position</code> attribute.</li> 
           <li>For single-line comments, the diff-positioned way of referencing comments for the <code>position</code> attribute.</li> 
          </ul> 
         </div> 
         <div class="extended-markdown note border rounded-1 mb-4 p-3 color-border-info color-bg-info f5"> 
          <p>An additional <code>reactions</code> object in the issue comment payload is currently available for developers to preview. During the preview period, the APIs may change without advance notice. Please see the <a href="https://developer.github.com/changes/2016-05-12-reactions-api-preview">blog post</a> for full details.</p> 
          <p>To access the API you must provide a custom <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/overview/media-types">media type</a> in the <code>Accept</code> header:</p> 
          <pre><code class="hljs language-shell">application/vnd.github.squirrel-girl-preview</code></pre> 
          <p>The <code>reactions</code> key will have the following payload where <code>url</code> can be used to construct the API location for <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/reference/reactions">listing and creating</a> reactions.</p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <hr> 
       </div> 
       <div> 
        <div>

         <h4>Notes</h4> 
         <ul class="mt-2"> 
          <li><a href="/en/developers/apps">Works with GitHub Apps</a></li> 
         </ul> 
         <h4 id="get-a-review-comment-for-a-pull-request-preview-notices"> Preview notices </h4> 
         <div class="extended-markdown note border rounded-1 mb-4 p-3 color-border-info color-bg-info f5"> 
          <p>Multi-line comments in a pull request diff is currently available for developers to preview. During the preview period, these response fields may change without advance notice. See the <a href="https://developer.github.com/changes/2019-10-03-multi-line-comments">blog post</a> for more information.</p> 
          <p>To create multi-line comments or see multi-line comments with the new supported fields during the preview period, you must provide a custom <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/overview/media-types">media type</a> in the <code>Accept</code> header:</p> 
          <pre><code class="hljs language-shell">application/vnd.github.comfort-fade-preview+json</code></pre> 
          <p>To show multi-line comment-supported fields in the response, use the <code>comfort-fade</code> preview header and the <code>line</code> parameter.</p> 
          <p>If you use the <code>comfort-fade</code> preview header, your response will show:</p> 
          <ul> 
           <li>For multi-line comments, values for <code>start_line</code>, <code>original_start_line</code>, <code>start_side</code>, <code>line</code>, <code>original_line</code>, and <code>side</code>.</li> 
           <li>For single-line comments, values for <code>line</code>, <code>original_line</code>, and <code>side</code> and a <code>null</code> value for <code>start_line</code>, <code>original_start_line</code>, and <code>start_side</code>.</li> 
          </ul> 
          <p>If you don't use the <code>comfort-fade</code> preview header, multi-line and single-line comments will appear the same way in the response with a single <code>position</code> attribute. Your response will show:</p> 
          <ul> 
           <li>For multi-line comments, the last line of the comment range for the <code>position</code> attribute.</li> 
           <li>For single-line comments, the diff-positioned way of referencing comments for the <code>position</code> attribute.</li> 
          </ul> 
         </div> 
         <div class="extended-markdown note border rounded-1 mb-4 p-3 color-border-info color-bg-info f5"> 
          <p>An additional <code>reactions</code> object in the issue comment payload is currently available for developers to preview. During the preview period, the APIs may change without advance notice. Please see the <a href="https://developer.github.com/changes/2016-05-12-reactions-api-preview">blog post</a> for full details.</p> 
          <p>To access the API you must provide a custom <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/overview/media-types">media type</a> in the <code>Accept</code> header:</p> 
          <pre><code class="hljs language-shell">application/vnd.github.squirrel-girl-preview</code></pre> 
          <p>The <code>reactions</code> key will have the following payload where <code>url</code> can be used to construct the API location for <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/reference/reactions">listing and creating</a> reactions.</p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <hr> 
       </div> 
       <div> 
        <div> 
         <h3 id="update-a-review-comment-for-a-pull-request" class="pt-3"> <a href="#update-a-review-comment-for-a-pull-request">Update a review comment for a pull request</a> </h3> 
         <p>Enables you to edit a review comment.</p> 
        </div> 
        <pre><code><span class="color-bg-info-inverse color-text-inverse rounded-1 px-2 py-1" style="text-transform: uppercase">patch</span> /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/comments/{comment_id}</code></pre> 
        <div> 
         <h4 id="update-a-review-comment-for-a-pull-request--parameters"> <a href="#update-a-review-comment-for-a-pull-request--parameters">Parameters</a> </h4> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Name</th> 
            <th>Type</th> 
            <th>In</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> <!--
            Previews require an `accept` header. These used to be documented
            as `operation.parameters` but have moved to `operation.x-github.previews`
          --> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>accept</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">header</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p> Setting to <code>application/vnd.github.v3+json</code> is recommended. <a href="#update-a-review-comment-for-a-pull-request-preview-notices"> See preview notice </a> </p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>owner</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>repo</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>comment_id</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>comment_id parameter</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>body</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p><strong>Required</strong>. The text of the reply to the review comment.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
         <h4 id="update-a-review-comment-for-a-pull-request--code-samples"> <a href="#update-a-review-comment-for-a-pull-request--code-samples">Code samples</a> </h4> 
         <h5> Shell </h5> 
         <pre><code class="hljs language-shell">curl \
  -X PATCH \
  -H "Accept: application/vnd.github.v3+json" \
  https://api.github.com/repos/octocat/hello-world/pulls/comments/42 \
  -d '{"body":"body"}'</code></pre>

         <h3 id="list-review-comments-on-a-pull-request" class="pt-3"> <a href="#list-review-comments-on-a-pull-request">List review comments on a pull request</a> </h3> 
         <p>Lists all review comments for a pull request. By default, review comments are in ascending order by ID.</p> 
        </div> 
        <pre><code><span class="color-bg-info-inverse color-text-inverse rounded-1 px-2 py-1" style="text-transform: uppercase">get</span> /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/{pull_number}/comments</code></pre> 
        <div> 
         <h4 id="list-review-comments-on-a-pull-request--parameters"> <a href="#list-review-comments-on-a-pull-request--parameters">Parameters</a> </h4> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Name</th> 
            <th>Type</th> 
            <th>In</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> <!--
            Previews require an `accept` header. These used to be documented
            as `operation.parameters` but have moved to `operation.x-github.previews`
          --> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>accept</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">header</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p> Setting to <code>application/vnd.github.v3+json</code> is recommended. <a href="#list-review-comments-on-a-pull-request-preview-notices"> See preview notices </a> </p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>owner</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>repo</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>pull_number</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>sort</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">query</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>One of <code>created</code> (when the repository was starred) or <code>updated</code> (when it was last pushed to).</p> Default: <code>created</code> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>direction</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">query</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>Can be either <code>asc</code> or <code>desc</code>. Ignored without <code>sort</code> parameter.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>since</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">query</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>Only show notifications updated after the given time. This is a timestamp in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISO_8601">ISO 8601</a> format: <code>YYYY-MM-DDTHH:MM:SSZ</code>.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>per_page</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">query</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>Results per page (max 100).</p> Default: <code>30</code> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>page</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">query</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>Page number of the results to fetch.</p> Default: <code>1</code> </td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table>

         <h4>Notes</h4> 
         <ul class="mt-2"> 
          <li><a href="/en/developers/apps">Works with GitHub Apps</a></li> 
         </ul> 
         <h4 id="list-review-comments-on-a-pull-request-preview-notices"> Preview notices </h4> 
         <div class="extended-markdown note border rounded-1 mb-4 p-3 color-border-info color-bg-info f5"> 
          <p>Multi-line comments in a pull request diff is currently available for developers to preview. During the preview period, these response fields may change without advance notice. See the <a href="https://developer.github.com/changes/2019-10-03-multi-line-comments">blog post</a> for more information.</p> 
          <p>To create multi-line comments or see multi-line comments with the new supported fields during the preview period, you must provide a custom <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/overview/media-types">media type</a> in the <code>Accept</code> header:</p> 
          <pre><code class="hljs language-shell">application/vnd.github.comfort-fade-preview+json</code></pre> 
          <p>To show multi-line comment-supported fields in the response, use the <code>comfort-fade</code> preview header and the <code>line</code> parameter.</p> 
          <p>If you use the <code>comfort-fade</code> preview header, your response will show:</p> 
          <ul> 
           <li>For multi-line comments, values for <code>start_line</code>, <code>original_start_line</code>, <code>start_side</code>, <code>line</code>, <code>original_line</code>, and <code>side</code>.</li> 
           <li>For single-line comments, values for <code>line</code>, <code>original_line</code>, and <code>side</code> and a <code>null</code> value for <code>start_line</code>, <code>original_start_line</code>, and <code>start_side</code>.</li> 
          </ul> 
          <p>If you don't use the <code>comfort-fade</code> preview header, multi-line and single-line comments will appear the same way in the response with a single <code>position</code> attribute. Your response will show:</p> 
          <ul> 
           <li>For multi-line comments, the last line of the comment range for the <code>position</code> attribute.</li> 
           <li>For single-line comments, the diff-positioned way of referencing comments for the <code>position</code> attribute.</li> 
          </ul> 
         </div> 
         <div class="extended-markdown note border rounded-1 mb-4 p-3 color-border-info color-bg-info f5"> 
          <p>An additional <code>reactions</code> object in the issue comment payload is currently available for developers to preview. During the preview period, the APIs may change without advance notice. Please see the <a href="https://developer.github.com/changes/2016-05-12-reactions-api-preview">blog post</a> for full details.</p> 
          <p>To access the API you must provide a custom <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/overview/media-types">media type</a> in the <code>Accept</code> header:</p> 
          <pre><code class="hljs language-shell">application/vnd.github.squirrel-girl-preview</code></pre> 
          <p>The <code>reactions</code> key will have the following payload where <code>url</code> can be used to construct the API location for <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/reference/reactions">listing and creating</a> reactions.</p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <hr> 
       </div> 
       <div> 
        <div> 
         <h3 id="create-a-review-comment-for-a-pull-request" class="pt-3"> <a href="#create-a-review-comment-for-a-pull-request">Create a review comment for a pull request</a> </h3> 
         <p>Creates a review comment in the pull request diff. To add a regular comment to a pull request timeline, see "<a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/reference/issues#create-an-issue-comment">Create an issue comment</a>." We recommend creating a review comment using <code>line</code>, <code>side</code>, and optionally <code>start_line</code> and <code>start_side</code> if your comment applies to more than one line in the pull request diff.</p> 
         <p>You can still create a review comment using the <code>position</code> parameter. When you use <code>position</code>, the <code>line</code>, <code>side</code>, <code>start_line</code>, and <code>start_side</code> parameters are not required. For more information, see the <a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/reference/pulls#create-a-review-comment-for-a-pull-request-preview-notices"><code>comfort-fade</code> preview notice</a>.</p> 
         <p><strong>Note:</strong> The position value equals the number of lines down from the first "@@" hunk header in the file you want to add a comment. The line just below the "@@" line is position 1, the next line is position 2, and so on. The position in the diff continues to increase through lines of whitespace and additional hunks until the beginning of a new file.</p> 
         <p>This endpoint triggers <a href="https://docs.github.com/en/github/managing-subscriptions-and-notifications-on-github/about-notifications">notifications</a>. Creating content too quickly using this endpoint may result in abuse rate limiting. See "<a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/overview/resources-in-the-rest-api#abuse-rate-limits">Abuse rate limits</a>" and "<a href="https://docs.github.com/rest/guides/best-practices-for-integrators#dealing-with-rate-limits">Dealing with abuse rate limits</a>" for details.</p> 
        </div> 
        <pre><code><span class="color-bg-info-inverse color-text-inverse rounded-1 px-2 py-1" style="text-transform: uppercase">post</span> /repos/{owner}/{repo}/pulls/{pull_number}/comments</code></pre> 
        <div> 
         <h4 id="create-a-review-comment-for-a-pull-request--parameters"> <a href="#create-a-review-comment-for-a-pull-request--parameters">Parameters</a> </h4> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Name</th> 
            <th>Type</th> 
            <th>In</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> <!--
            Previews require an `accept` header. These used to be documented
            as `operation.parameters` but have moved to `operation.x-github.previews`
          --> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>accept</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">header</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p> Setting to <code>application/vnd.github.v3+json</code> is recommended. <a href="#create-a-review-comment-for-a-pull-request-preview-notices"> See preview notice </a> </p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>owner</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>repo</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>pull_number</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">path</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>body</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p><strong>Required</strong>. The text of the review comment.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>commit_id</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>The SHA of the commit needing a comment. Not using the latest commit SHA may render your comment outdated if a subsequent commit modifies the line you specify as the <code>position</code>.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>path</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p>The relative path to the file that necessitates a comment.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>position</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p><strong>Required without <code>comfort-fade</code> preview</strong>. The position in the diff where you want to add a review comment. Note this value is not the same as the line number in the file. For help finding the position value, read the note above.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>side</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p><strong>Required with <code>comfort-fade</code> preview</strong>. In a split diff view, the side of the diff that the pull request's changes appear on. Can be <code>LEFT</code> or <code>RIGHT</code>. Use <code>LEFT</code> for deletions that appear in red. Use <code>RIGHT</code> for additions that appear in green or unchanged lines that appear in white and are shown for context. For a multi-line comment, side represents whether the last line of the comment range is a deletion or addition. For more information, see "<a href="https://help.github.com/en/articles/about-comparing-branches-in-pull-requests#diff-view-options">Diff view options</a>" in the GitHub Help documentation.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>line</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p><strong>Required with <code>comfort-fade</code> preview</strong>. The line of the blob in the pull request diff that the comment applies to. For a multi-line comment, the last line of the range that your comment applies to.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>start_line</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p><strong>Required when using multi-line comments</strong>. To create multi-line comments, you must use the <code>comfort-fade</code> preview header. The <code>start_line</code> is the first line in the pull request diff that your multi-line comment applies to. To learn more about multi-line comments, see "<a href="https://help.github.com/en/articles/commenting-on-a-pull-request#adding-line-comments-to-a-pull-request">Commenting on a pull request</a>" in the GitHub Help documentation.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>start_side</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">string</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> <p><strong>Required when using multi-line comments</strong>. To create multi-line comments, you must use the <code>comfort-fade</code> preview header. The <code>start_side</code> is the starting side of the diff that the comment applies to. Can be <code>LEFT</code> or <code>RIGHT</code>. To learn more about multi-line comments, see "<a href="https://help.github.com/en/articles/commenting-on-a-pull-request#adding-line-comments-to-a-pull-request">Commenting on a pull request</a>" in the GitHub Help documentation. See <code>side</code> in this table for additional context.</p> </td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>in_reply_to</code></td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">integer</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70">body</td> 
            <td class="opacity-70"> </td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table>
